# Darwin Backlog

This document is the execution roadmap for Darwin. It is intentionally priority-based, not merely historical. The current guiding rule is:

- finish `Darwin.WebAdmin` and the admin/backend workflows needed for real SME operations first
- keep mobile-used API paths stable
- return to broader front-office and non-critical expansion after the operational core is ready

Status terms used below:

- `Completed`
- `In Progress`
- `Planned / Near-term`
- `Future / Later phase`

## 0. Cross-Chat Coordination Ledger

This section is the shared handoff ledger between the active implementation chats:

- `Web`
- `WebAdmin`
- `Mobile`

Rules:

- before starting a new slice, each chat should review this ledger
- each handoff should be recorded as one flat entry and updated in place when acknowledged or closed
- use these statuses:
  - `Open`
  - `Acked`
  - `Closed`
  - `Superseded`

Entry format:

- `[Status] YYYY-MM-DD | From: <Web|WebAdmin|Mobile> | To: <Web|WebAdmin|Mobile> | Topic: <short topic> | Message: <concrete handoff> | Expected action: <what the receiving chat should do>`

Active entries:

- `Testing`: WebAdmin now has a dedicated `Darwin.WebAdmin.Tests` project in the solution using `WebApplicationFactory<Program>` to compile the real Razor app and run no-database smoke checks for unauthenticated admin redirects, authenticated admin fragment permission allow/deny boundaries, forwarded HTTPS proxy handling, HSTS on non-local HTTPS hosts, login/register/2FA public auth surfaces, query-string and cookie-driven auth-page localization, CultureController CSRF/open-redirect defenses, security headers on success and 404 responses, anti-forgery token and secure cookie rendering, runtime rejection of tokenless/invalid-token public account POST mutations across login, register, 2FA, WebAuthn begin/finish, and logout, successful anti-forgery header validation for HTMX-style account logout, and self-hosted static asset loading for vendor/runtime files.
- `Testing`: WebAdmin now also has an authenticated DB-backed smoke-test lane using an isolated EF Core InMemory `DarwinDbContext` wired through the real `IAppDbContext`; the dashboard plus identity, catalog/CMS, business operations, billing, inventory, loyalty, media, orders, and shipping list pages render through real handlers/views under authorization, with seeded business/loyalty context for tenant-scoped screens; the lane caught and closed the missing `GetUserOpsSummaryHandler` DI registration.
- `Testing`: WebAdmin DB-backed smoke coverage now reaches editor and seeded-entity GET flows as well: media/shipping/billing/business/loyalty create editors render with anti-forgery tokens, and seeded business/loyalty detail, setup, support, readiness, communication-audit, subscription, and edit-program pages render through real handlers and Razor views.
- `Testing`: WebAdmin DB-backed smoke coverage now exercises HTMX GET behavior directly: list/detail/dashboard fragment partials render without full layouts or shared scripts, editor partials keep anti-forgery tokens, and business setup/support, SiteSettings, MobileOperations, billing, loyalty, orders, media, shipping, and communications partial refreshes stay covered under the real `HX-Request` header.
- `Testing`: WebAdmin runtime CSRF smoke coverage now includes authenticated admin mutation endpoints across the major operator workspaces: tokenless HTMX POSTs to media, shipping, billing, business lifecycle/support, BusinessCommunications transport tests/retries, SiteSettings, loyalty, mobile operations, orders, inventory, users, catalog/CMS, and CRM handlers are rejected with BadRequest before handlers run, keeping the source-level anti-forgery rules backed by the hosted app.
- `Testing`: WebAdmin positive anti-forgery smoke coverage now extracts real editor tokens and posts them back to representative media, shipping, billing, business, and loyalty create handlers, verifying valid admin tokens pass CSRF filtering and reach handler/model validation instead of only testing tokenless rejection.
- `Testing`: WebAdmin positive mutation smoke coverage now includes real DB-backed Billing Plan, Payment, FinancialAccount, Expense, JournalEntry, Warehouse, Supplier, StockLevel, StockTransfer, PurchaseOrder, Customer, Lead, CustomerSegment, Opportunity, User, UserRole assignment, UserChangeEmail, UserChangePassword, Role, Permission, RolePermission assignment, AddOnGroup, Brand, CMS Page, Category, Product, ShippingMethod, Order status change, OrderPayment, OrderShipment, OrderInvoice, OrderRefund, Business, BusinessLocation, BusinessInvitation, BusinessMember, LoyaltyProgram, BusinessCampaign, LoyaltyRewardTier, and LoyaltyAccount flows: tests seed stable catalog/loyalty/member/inventory/identity/order dependencies, create balanced finance accounts before journal entries, create warehouse/supplier dependencies before inventory operations, create a CRM customer before its opportunity, post real UserRoles/RolePermissions/Order RowVersion values for assignment/status updates, replace outbound email with a no-op sender in the test host, post valid HTMX forms with editor anti-forgery tokens, assert `HX-Redirect` success paths, and verify created/changed/assigned records appear in filtered list, grid, detail, or editor views; this also closed ShippingMethod create/update async-validation handling for unique-name rules and fixed CRM Opportunity create/edit currency binding.
- `Security hardening`: WebAdmin account returnUrl handling now uses `Url.IsLocalUrl` instead of broad relative-URI checks, and the login/auth layout surfaces avoid reflecting unsafe external returnUrl query values into login, passkey, or culture-switch forms; smoke tests pin the external-returnUrl non-reflection path.
- `Build quality`: WebAdmin Razor compilation is now exercised by the new smoke project, which exposed and closed previously hidden compile errors in AddOnGroups, Billing, MobileOperations, Permissions/Roles, ShippingMethods, Inventory action shells, Business member/user handoffs, TaxCompliance nullable ids, and Business communication readiness summary wiring.
- `Security hardening`: WebAdmin authentication and anti-forgery cookies are now explicitly secure/admin-scoped: auth and anti-forgery cookies are `HttpOnly`, `SameSite=Lax`, `SecurePolicy=Always`, and anti-forgery uses the HTMX-compatible `RequestVerificationToken` header; source tests guard these cookie/token defaults.
- `Security hardening`: WebAdmin now emits strict self-hosted security headers before static files, including a `Content-Security-Policy` without `unsafe-inline`/`unsafe-eval`, plus `X-Content-Type-Options`, `Referrer-Policy`, and `Permissions-Policy`; source tests guard header ordering and policy shape.
- `Security hardening`: WebAdmin production proxy readiness is now wired with `ForwardedHeadersOptions` for `X-Forwarded-For` and `X-Forwarded-Proto`, optional configured known proxies/networks, and `UseForwardedHeaders()` before HTTPS redirection so HSTS, redirects, and secure cookies can honor reverse-proxy scheme forwarding.
- `Security hardening`: WebAdmin vendor frontend dependencies are now self-hosted under `wwwroot/lib` instead of loaded from CDNs; shared layouts and validation partials use local versioned Bootstrap, Font Awesome, jQuery, HTMX, Quill, and validation assets, and source tests guard against external script/style regressions.
- `Security hardening`: WebAdmin self-hosted vendor dependencies now have an auditable `wwwroot/lib/vendor-manifest.json` with version, license, source, and file mappings for Bootstrap, Font Awesome, HTMX, jQuery, jQuery Validation, unobtrusive validation, and Quill; source tests guard manifest completeness alongside asset presence.
- `Security hardening`: WebAdmin Razor views are now cleaner for CSP hardening: all inline `style=` attributes were replaced with local `admin.css` utility classes, and source tests now guard against inline style regressions alongside the existing inline script, unsafe rendering, and inline event guards.
- `Security hardening`: WebAdmin AddOnGroups options editor no longer uses an inline script; localized option/value row HTML now lives in Razor `<template>` markup and the add/remove behavior is handled by the local versioned `add-on-groups.js` asset, bringing WebAdmin Razor inline script blocks to zero.
- `Security hardening`: WebAdmin Page/Product Quill editors and the User address modal now use local versioned JavaScript assets (`content-editors.js` and `admin-core.js`) instead of Razor inline scripts; source tests guard those editor shells against inline script regressions.
- `Security hardening`: WebAdmin Account login passkey placeholder plus CRM opportunity/customer dynamic line editors now use local delegated JavaScript (`admin-core.js` and `dynamic-lines.js`) instead of page/partial inline scripts; source tests guard those surfaces against regressions.
- `Security hardening`: WebAdmin Media copy-url and ShippingMethods rate-tier JavaScript now live in local versioned assets (`wwwroot/js/media.js` and `wwwroot/js/shipping-methods.js`); Media and ShippingMethods views are guarded against inline script regressions while localized labels stay in data attributes.
- `[Closed] 2026-03-31 | From: Web | To: WebAdmin | Topic: CMS main navigation seed | Message: Darwin.Web needed a published public menu named main-navigation plus stable CMS/catalog seed content so shell and storefront slices could stop depending on hidden fallback-only behavior. | Expected action: seed and publish the menu/content in WebAdmin/backend.`
- `[Closed] 2026-03-31 | From: WebAdmin | To: Web | Topic: CMS/storefront dependencies confirmed | Message: main-navigation is ready, CMS published page slugs such as ueber-uns and faq are available, representative catalog seed with real primary media exists, menu badge/icon/group metadata is not yet contract, publish rules are confirmed, and missing-image policy must be handled in Darwin.Web. | Expected action: treat main-navigation as the primary source, keep fallback nav emergency-only, consume CMS/catalog directly from WebApi, make fetch failures visible, and keep backlog/docs aligned with these confirmed contracts.`
- `[Closed] 2026-04-21 | From: WebAdmin | To: Web,Mobile | Topic: member shipment tracking URL contract | Message: member order shipment snapshots now expose an optional DHL \`trackingUrl\` alongside the existing tracking number and shipment lifecycle timestamps. | Expected action: Darwin.Web member order detail and Darwin.Mobile.Consumer member commerce order detail now consume \`trackingUrl\` through direct tracking CTA rails instead of leaving the field as an unused backend-only contract.`
- `[Closed] 2026-03-31 | From: WebAdmin | To: Web | Topic: Phone verification and multi-channel communication contracts | Message: backend now exposes canonical current-user phone verification over SMS or WhatsApp, persisted preferred-channel plus fallback policy in site settings, customizable phone-verification text templates, customizable provider-backed SMS/WhatsApp transport-test templates, and a new CustomerProfile flag for phone-number confirmation. | Expected action: when building account/profile UX, consume the new profile field and the request/confirm phone-verification endpoints instead of inventing a web-only mobile-verification flow.`
- `[Closed] 2026-03-31 | From: WebAdmin | To: Mobile | Topic: Phone verification and multi-channel communication contracts | Message: backend now exposes canonical current-user phone verification over SMS or WhatsApp, persisted preferred-channel plus fallback policy in site settings, customizable phone-verification text templates, customizable provider-backed SMS/WhatsApp transport-test templates, and a new CustomerProfile flag for phone-number confirmation. | Expected action: during the mobile review/use-case pass, consume the new profile field and the request/confirm phone-verification endpoints instead of keeping any app-local verification workflow assumptions.`
- `[Acked] 2026-04-01 | From: WebAdmin | To: Web,Mobile | Topic: de/en localization baseline in admin | Message: WebAdmin now enforces a settings-driven `de-DE`/`en-US` request-localization baseline with cookie/query-string culture switching and bilingual shared/admin-auth chrome. Site Settings and Business Communications have started moving onto the same bilingual operator surface. | Expected action: assume German and English are the current platform languages, keep frontend/mobile wording compatible with that baseline, and treat future languages as additive rather than redefining the initial contract.`
- `[Acked] 2026-04-01 | From: Web | To: WebAdmin,Mobile | Topic: resource-backed front-office localization baseline | Message: Darwin.Web now has a resource-bundle localization slice under `src/Darwin.Web/src/localization/resources` for shared shell, catalog, storefront-commerce, account self-service, member commerce, and loyalty surfaces including discovery, pre-join detail, and signed-in business detail. Culture switching still uses the de/en platform baseline, but new frontend languages should be added as new resource bundles rather than in-component dictionaries. | Expected action: keep future shared wording and language additions compatible with the additive `de-DE` / `en-US` baseline and avoid introducing app-local hardcoded copy paths for common front-office/member wording.`
- `[Closed] 2026-04-02 | From: Web | To: WebAdmin | Topic: localized slug mapping for SEO alternates | Message: Darwin.Web now resolves CMS/product detail `hreflang` alternates by matching canonical public page/product ids across the current `de-DE` / `en-US` public sets, so localized detail-page alternates no longer depend on slug parity guesses. A dedicated localized-slug map contract is no longer required for the current two-language baseline, though richer multilingual content operations may still justify one later. | Expected action: none for the current baseline; keep public page/product ids stable across language variants.`
- `[Superseded] 2026-04-02 | From: Web | To: WebAdmin | Topic: catalog search and facet contract expansion | Message: Darwin.Web no longer relies only on page-local text filtering on `/catalog`; real public query search is now wired through the current product-listing contract. The remaining gap is no longer baseline search itself but richer facet/filter/sort projections for scalable catalog discovery. | Expected action: decide whether public catalog should expose facet counts, brand filters, and stronger server-side sort/filter projections so Darwin.Web can move beyond query search plus client-side browse lenses.`
- `[Superseded] 2026-04-02 | From: Web | To: WebAdmin | Topic: CMS search contract expansion | Message: Darwin.Web no longer relies only on page-local text filtering on `/cms`; real public query search is now wired through the current CMS-listing contract. The remaining gap is richer result metadata and grouping/topic curation, not baseline public CMS search itself. | Expected action: decide whether public CMS should expose richer search/result metadata or editorial grouping signals beyond the now-delivered query-search baseline.`
- `[Closed] 2026-04-02 | From: Web | To: WebAdmin | Topic: payment-attempt ordering metadata for confirmation/member commerce | Message: Darwin.Web can now render storefront confirmation and member commerce payment states, but the public/member payment snapshots only expose `status` and optional `paidAtUtc`. When multiple payment attempts exist, web cannot safely derive the latest attempt state without either attempt ordering guarantees or a creation timestamp on each payment snapshot. The current web fix now avoids showing a stale inferred "latest" status, but richer route summaries still need canonical payment-attempt ordering metadata from WebApi. | Expected action: public/member payment snapshots now expose canonical `createdAtUtc`, so web/mobile can display the current payment-attempt state without heuristic guessing.` 

## 1. Current Delivery Focus

### PostgreSQL Primary Persistence Track

- `Completed foundation`: PostgreSQL is now the preferred local/default database provider while the current SQL Server infrastructure and migrations remain available for customer deployments that still require SQL Server.
- `Completed foundation`: the provider-specific project is named `Darwin.Infrastructure.PostgreSql`; it references the existing `Darwin.Infrastructure` DbContext/model instead of copying mappings, and owns PostgreSQL registration plus PostgreSQL-specific migrations.
- `Completed foundation`: the SQL Server provider now has the explicit project name `Darwin.Infrastructure.SqlServer`; it owns SQL Server registration while the existing SQL Server migration lane remains in `Darwin.Infrastructure.Migrations` for compatibility.
- `Completed foundation`: runtime provider selection now lives in the neutral `Darwin.Infrastructure.PersistenceProviders` project so PostgreSQL and SQL Server provider projects do not depend on each other.
- `Completed foundation`: WebAdmin, WebApi, and Worker now use a single runtime selector through configuration (`Persistence:Provider`) and can choose `PostgreSql` or `SqlServer` without code changes per customer.
- `Completed foundation`: Docker Desktop development services now provide PostgreSQL plus pgAdmin; local defaults use `ConnectionStrings:PostgreSql` while leaving the existing SQL Server connection string in place.
- `Completed foundation`: PostgreSQL initial migration was generated, applied to the Docker PostgreSQL database, and validated with WebAdmin development startup seeding.
- `Completed foundation`: the first provider-specific EF issues are handled: SQL Server-only column types were removed from shared mappings, filtered index SQL is normalized for PostgreSQL, and `RowVersion` is provider-aware so SQL Server keeps native rowversion while PostgreSQL uses client-managed concurrency bytes.
- `Completed foundation`: module schema naming was normalized for application tables that previously fell into provider defaults (`public`/`dbo`), including communication audits, shipping rates, catalog option/media tables, shipments, shipment lines, carrier events, and refunds.
- `Completed foundation`: PostgreSQL now enables `pg_trgm` plus GIN trigram indexes for high-value text search surfaces in catalog, CMS, business, and identity data.
- `Planned / Near-term`: continue auditing provider-specific EF assumptions such as string comparison/collation behavior, decimal precision, JSON/text columns, date/time handling, and future migration SQL before calling PostgreSQL production-ready.
- `Completed documentation`: `DarwinTesting.md` now records the provider-selection, PostgreSQL migration/seed, provider SQL-type, filtered-index, and RowVersion coverage backlog without expanding test projects in this implementation slice.
- `Future / Later phase`: after PostgreSQL is stable as primary, back-port future schema changes to the SQL Server migration lane when customers need SQL Server deployments.

### Storefront Readiness Audit

- `Completed foundation`: the local development seed now covers the minimum storefront graph needed for realistic front-office testing: seeded identity roles and demo users with default addresses, 10+ businesses, 10+ business locations, 20+ CMS pages, 10+ marketing campaigns, 20+ catalog products across multiple categories, shipping methods plus rates, pricing promotions such as `WELCOME10` / `FIVER` / `SEASONAL`, sample carts, and seeded orders with payments, shipments, and refunds
- `Completed foundation`: Darwin.Web and Darwin.WebApi now provide an end-to-end non-loyalty storefront path for catalog browse, product detail, add-to-cart, cart mutation, coupon apply/clear, checkout intent creation, order placement, hosted payment handoff creation, payment completion reconciliation, and order confirmation rendering
- `Completed foundation`: integration smoke coverage now protects that seeded storefront baseline directly by checking public discovery seed availability plus an anonymous commerce flow from cart mutation and seeded coupon application through checkout, payment intent creation, payment completion, and confirmation
- `Planned / Near-term`: keep auditing remaining tail-level storefront gaps against seeded data so backlog status reflects concrete missing behavior, not stale in-progress labels
- `Completed foundation`: local hosted-checkout readiness is now wired end-to-end for storefront development: `Darwin.WebApi` development settings point payment handoff back to the local web app, and `Darwin.Web` now exposes a real `/mock-checkout` route that can return explicit success, cancellation, and failure outcomes into confirmation-finalize reconciliation
- `Completed foundation`: the non-email communication-audit guidance/state vocabulary now lives in a shared `Darwin.Application` catalog consumed by both `GetChannelDispatchActivityHandler` and the `BusinessCommunicationsController` / `ChannelAudits` surface, so SMS/WhatsApp operator guidance no longer depends on duplicated sentence-level English matching before localization can apply
- `Completed foundation`: the non-email audit workspace now also overlays unmatched queued `ChannelDispatchOperation` rows from the worker outbox, so admin operators can see SMS/WhatsApp dispatches that are still waiting on background processing or failed before a final `ChannelDispatchAudit` row exists
- `Completed foundation`: setup and merchant-readiness invitation surfaces now preserve business-scoped failed-invitation audit handoffs, including recipient-level setup preview links and per-business readiness links, so invitation delivery triage stays precise outside the invitation queue as well
- `Completed foundation`: the business communication profile current-flows action now opens business-scoped failed invitation audits with an explicit failed-invitation CTA, so communication-profile triage follows the same delivery-failure path as setup, readiness, and invitation queue surfaces
- `Completed foundation`: the Business Communications operations index now exposes failed invitation email audits from both primary runtime/provider action rails, closing the remaining communication-ops gap where operators could open pending invitations but not the matching failed delivery queue directly
- `Completed foundation`: Business Communications runtime execution health now counts failed invitation emails alongside activation, password reset, and admin-test failures on both the operations index and per-business communication profile, with direct failed-invitation audit handoffs kept visible in the same action rails
- `Completed foundation`: failed invitation delivery counts now flow through support and communication summary DTOs into Support Queue, Merchant Readiness, Home communication/support cards, and Business Setup runtime-execution summaries, so top-level readiness no longer hides invitation delivery failures while lower-level communication screens expose them
- `Completed foundation`: the Home business-support card now uses `BusinessSupport` as the failed-email source for support fragments and shows business-scoped failed invitation, activation, password-reset, and admin-test counts in the selected-business snapshot, with audit links carrying the selected `businessId`
- `Completed foundation`: the Home business-operations card now uses selected-business support counts for runtime email-delivery health and scopes invitation/member plus email/SMS/WhatsApp remediation links to the selected business, so dashboard-level go-live triage no longer mixes global delivery failures into a selected tenant context
- `Completed foundation`: the Home communication-ops fragment now hydrates `BusinessSupport` alongside communication readiness, and the selected-business communication rail scopes retry-blocked, repeated-failure, failed-flow, action-blocked, escalation, and phone-verification drilldowns to the selected business instead of refreshing into global audit queues
- `Completed foundation`: the business communication profile now keeps activation and locked/password-reset member handoffs inside the selected business member queue instead of sending operators to global user queues, aligning profile-level runtime triage with its business-scoped failed-email and channel audit links
- `Completed foundation`: the Business Communications index now exposes row-level tenant-scoped remediation handoffs for email audits, failed invitation emails, SMS/WhatsApp audits, pending invitations, pending activations, and locked/password-reset members, so operators can jump from the business list directly into scoped support queues without opening the profile first
- `Completed foundation`: Business Setup and Merchant Readiness row-level runtime-execution rails now keep pending-activation and locked/password-reset member handoffs inside the selected business member queue, while aggregate readiness cards continue to use global user queues intentionally for fleet-wide triage
- `Completed foundation`: support failed-email rows and selected-business Home support/communication cards now keep activation/password-reset member remediation, failed-flow audits, retry/chain follow-up, and channel escalation drill-ins scoped to the affected or selected business, leaving only explicit email/account lookup fallbacks as global user searches
- `Completed foundation`: business-member pending-activation alerts and non-email channel-audit identity-lifecycle follow-ups now preserve tenant context by routing activation/password-reset remediation to `Businesses/Members` whenever a business id is available, with global `Users` queues retained only for aggregate dashboards, mobile-linked identity review, and tenantless lookup fallbacks
- `Completed foundation`: Mobile Operations now accepts and preserves a `businessId` device filter, so business communication profiles, channel-audit phone-verification rows, and setup mobile/security handoffs can open mobile-device triage scoped to the selected or affected business instead of dropping operators into the fleet-wide device queue
- `Completed foundation`: business member, invitation, setup-preview, staff-access-badge, failed-email, email-audit, merchant-readiness row, and loyalty mobile handoffs now carry `businessId` into Mobile Operations; fleet-wide Mobile Operations links are intentionally left only on aggregate/global admin surfaces
- `Completed foundation`: Support Queue and Merchant Readiness now accept a `businessId` workspace scope, filter summaries/failed email handoffs/readiness rows for the selected business, and preserve that scope from member, invitation, location, staff badge, and editor-shell pivots
- `Completed foundation`: setup shell, business forms, owner-override audits, and subscription helper pivots now preserve `businessId` for both HTMX and progressive href handoffs into Support Queue and Merchant Readiness, so tenant-scoped remediation no longer falls back to aggregate queues when JavaScript is unavailable or links are opened directly
- `Security hardening`: source-contract tests now pin the progressive `asp-route-businessId` side of those scoped Support Queue and Merchant Readiness handoffs, so future HTMX-only fixes cannot silently regress direct-link or no-JavaScript navigation back to aggregate support queues
- `Security hardening`: Businesses self-navigation, Support Queue fragments, merchant-readiness/support aggregate communications and finance pivots, plus SiteSettings and MobileOperations BusinessCommunications/Businesses pivots now route no-arg HTMX links through explicit global URL helpers while scoped route-value drill-ins remain unchanged
- `Security hardening`: AddOnGroups workspace, editor back link, and product/category/brand/variant attachment GET handoffs now use explicit URL helpers for index/create/edit/attach navigation, leaving the AddOnGroups view folder free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links and covered by source-contract tests
- `Security hardening`: CRM pipeline workspaces now route Overview, Leads, Opportunities, Segments, and lead/opportunity/segment editor follow-up/back GET handoffs through explicit URL helpers, leaving the sales-pipeline CRM views free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links while invoice/customer finance flows remain a separate cleanup slice
- `Security hardening`: CRM invoice/customer workspaces and their editor shells now route invoice/customer queues, tax/localization settings, opportunity/segment handoffs, order/payment drill-ins, payment queue follow-ups, user/customer row actions, and interaction/consent/segment fragments through explicit URL helpers, leaving the high-traffic CRM invoice/customer cluster free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links while preserving POST mutations
- `Security hardening`: Roles and Permissions workspaces, editor back links, delegated-support rails, and role-permission handoffs now use explicit URL helpers for index/create/edit/permission/user-filter navigation, leaving both identity admin view folders free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links and pinned by source-contract tests
- `Security hardening`: Users workspace and user edit/change-email/change-password editor shells now route lifecycle queues, failed activation/password-reset audits, mobile/loyalty pivots, create/edit/roles/credential changes, and return-to-index back links through explicit URL helpers, leaving the Users view folder free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links while preserving identity mutation POSTs and delete modal actions
- `Security hardening`: Inventory StockTransfers, PurchaseOrders, and Suppliers workspaces now route queue filters, reset/search forms, create/edit actions, stock-level pivots, supplier/purchase-order handoffs, and row drill-ins through explicit URL helpers, removing the three largest Inventory raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` clusters while preserving pager/query contracts
- `Security hardening`: Billing FinancialAccounts, Expenses, JournalEntries, and Plans workspaces now route search/reset flows, queue chips, create/edit actions, account/expense/journal/payment pivots, supplier drill-ins, and row follow-ups through explicit URL helpers, removing the largest Billing finance raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` clusters while preserving pager/query and POST mutation contracts
- `Security hardening`: Orders ReturnsQueue, Details, and `_ShipmentsGrid` now route return filters, refund/shipment queue follow-ups, order operation shells, tax/shipping settings pivots, tab fragment loaders, and shipment refund/remediation actions through explicit URL helpers, removing the largest remaining Orders raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` clusters while preserving status-change and DHL-label POST mutation contracts
- `Security hardening`: Inventory VariantLedger, StockLevels, and Warehouses now route ledger filters, stock-level search/reset/queue chips, create/edit/adjust/reserve/release/return actions, warehouse filters, and stock-level/ledger pivots through explicit URL helpers, clearing the remaining high-count Inventory raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` clusters while preserving pager/query and mutation contracts
- `Security hardening`: Loyalty Programs, Accounts, Campaigns, RewardTiers, ScanSessions, Redemptions, account creation, point adjustment, and editor forms now route workspace filters, cross-workspace pivots, create/edit/detail/back links, mobile/provider-review follow-ups, reward-tier handoffs, and account adjustments through explicit URL helpers, leaving the Loyalty view folder free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links while preserving loyalty mutation POST contracts
- `Security hardening`: Media and Orders index workspaces, Catalog/CMS list workspaces (`Brands`, `Categories`, `Products`, `Pages`), Orders payment/invoice/refund grids, and CRM customer fragments now route search/reset flows, queue chips, create/edit/detail actions, payment/refund/invoice drill-ins, tax/customer follow-ups, and interaction/consent/segment loaders through explicit URL helpers, reducing remaining WebAdmin raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links to isolated one-off editor/back fragments while preserving POST mutation contracts
- `Security hardening`: the final one-off WebAdmin raw GET links are now closed across Billing finance/payment editor backs, Inventory stock/reservation/transfer/supplier/warehouse editor backs, Media/Brand/Category/Page/Product form backs, Orders payment/invoice/refund/shipment create-shell backs, CRM lead/opportunity fragment loaders, and Home dashboard refresh cards; WebAdmin Razor views now scan clean with zero raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links while POST mutation contracts and delete data-actions remain unchanged
- `Security hardening`: ShippingMethods workspace, editor shell, inline remediation rails, queue filters, shipment queue handoffs, and shipping settings pivots now use explicit URL helpers, leaving the ShippingMethods view folder free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links and covered by source-contract tests
- `Security hardening`: Billing Payments workspace and shared payment form now route settings, scoped payment queues, refund queues, webhook queues, order/customer/user/invoice drill-ins, and refund actions through explicit URL helpers, leaving both high-traffic payment views free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links and covered by source-contract tests
- `Security hardening`: Billing Refunds and Webhooks workspaces now route scoped refund/payment queues, aggregate webhook queues, payment settings, tax/invoice follow-ups, and order/customer/payment drill-ins through explicit URL helpers, leaving the finance triage quartet (`Payments`, `_PaymentForm`, `Refunds`, `Webhooks`) free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links and covered by source-contract tests
- `Security hardening`: Billing TaxCompliance now routes tax settings, CRM customer/invoice filters, order payment-issue follow-ups, invoice/customer/order/payment row drill-ins, and opportunity lookups through explicit URL helpers, completing the high-traffic Billing triage cleanup with no raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links left in Payments, payment form, Refunds, Webhooks, or TaxCompliance
- `Security hardening`: MobileOperations workspace header rails, go-live remediation cards, onboarding/transport actions, loyalty follow-ups, fleet filters, device row drill-ins, and remediation state pivots now use explicit URL helpers, leaving `MobileOperations/Index` free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links while preserving scoped business support and aggregate loyalty/user/provider-review handoffs
- `Security hardening`: Orders ShipmentsQueue now routes shipment queue filters, fulfillment/order detail drill-ins, shipping settings pivots, ShippingMethods remediation links, return/refund follow-ups, and add-shipment actions through explicit URL helpers, leaving the shipments queue workspace free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links while preserving DHL label generation as a POST mutation
- `Security hardening`: BusinessCommunications Index now routes transport/settings pivots, setup-only filters, email/channel audit queues, user/invitation remediation links, channel-family drill-ins, failed audit follow-ups, and business row actions through explicit URL helpers, leaving the communications operations index free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links while preserving test-send POST mutations
- `Security hardening`: BusinessCommunications ChannelAudits now routes support/settings pivots, channel audit filter chips, provider and exact-chain drill-ins, channel-family actions, mobile/user remediation links, business-member follow-ups, and row-level support/profile actions through explicit URL helpers, leaving the SMS/WhatsApp audit workspace free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links while preserving resend/test POST mutations
- `Security hardening`: BusinessCommunications Details now routes profile rails, setup/readiness/support pivots, member/invitation remediation, email audit filters, channel audit drill-ins, settings/mobile/user links, channel-family actions, and template/resend follow-ups through explicit URL helpers, leaving the business communication profile free of raw GET `Url.Action` handoffs while preserving send-test POST mutations
- `Security hardening`: BusinessCommunications EmailAudits now routes support/settings pivots, retry/follow-up/chain filters, flow playbooks, business profile drill-ins, phone-verification channel handoffs, exact-chain links, invitation/member remediation, user/mobile pivots, and row-level support/profile actions through explicit URL helpers, leaving the email audit workspace free of raw GET `Url.Action` handoffs while preserving retry/send-test POST mutations
- `Security hardening`: Businesses setup shell now routes setup header actions, owner/location/invitation remediation, operational-status pivots, readiness/support rails, communication defaults, billing/subscription follow-ups, preview fragments, mobile/security handoffs, and footer actions through explicit URL helpers, removing the largest remaining raw GET `Url.Action` cluster from WebAdmin while preserving setup/provision POST mutations
- `Security hardening`: Businesses MerchantReadiness now routes support/header actions, operational and readiness summary filters, user/email/channel audit remediation, CRM invoice filters, row identity/setup/subscription drill-ins, member/invitation conditional links, mobile/security handoffs, and billing follow-ups through explicit URL helpers, leaving the readiness workspace free of raw GET `Url.Action` handoffs
- `Security hardening`: Businesses Index now routes create/header actions, attention/operational/readiness summary filters, user and failed-email remediation, CRM invoice filters, row profile/member/location/invitation/subscription actions, communication drill-ins, and billing follow-ups through explicit URL helpers, leaving the business list workspace free of raw GET `Url.Action` handoffs while preserving delete data-actions
- `Security hardening`: Businesses SupportQueue failed-email fragment now routes failed-audit entry points, business/profile/user drill-ins, flow-specific invitation/member remediation, retry/chain/repeated-failure filters, communication/channel audits, merchant-readiness, subscription/billing/finance follow-ups, mobile operations, and policy settings through explicit URL helpers, leaving the failed-email support fragment free of raw GET `Url.Action` handoffs
- `Security hardening`: Businesses SupportQueue shell, summary fragment, and attention-business fragment now route header pivots, summary refresh/cards, lifecycle/readiness/governance chips, failed-flow/user/mobile drill-ins, row remediation, communication audits, merchant-readiness, finance, and billing follow-ups through explicit URL helpers, leaving the SupportQueue workspace cluster free of raw GET `Url.Action` handoffs

- `Security hardening`: Businesses editor shell, member editor shell, staff-access badge, owner-override audits, and locations workspaces now route conditional member/invitation pivots, setup/readiness/support rails, location/member/invitation create/edit actions, user/mobile/loyalty drill-ins, owner-override follow-ups, and filtered location/member queues through explicit URL helpers, leaving the editor/location/owner-governance cluster free of raw GET `Url.Action` handoffs while preserving POST mutations and delete data-actions
- `Security hardening`: Businesses form, setup preview, and location/member/invitation editor fragments now route owner guidance, active-state remediation, management footer pivots, queue-return links, setup/readiness/support rails, failed-invitation audit follow-ups, pending-activation/locked member shortcuts, mobile/user/loyalty drill-ins, and invitation status badges through explicit URL helpers; the Businesses view folder is now free of raw `hx-get="@Url.Action(...)"` links, while Users role support rails and Loyalty account detail header actions were also aligned with helper-backed navigation
- `Security hardening`: SiteSettings editor shell now routes communications policy, pending invitations, user lifecycle filters, email/channel audit playbooks, shipping method filters, shipment queues, mobile/loyalty handoffs, and global operations pivots through explicit URL helpers, removing the largest remaining single WebAdmin raw GET `Url.Action` cluster while preserving the settings POST contract
- `Completed foundation`: the main business editor shell now also preserves `businessId` across its operational-status, onboarding-checklist, next-action, and incomplete-setup Support Queue/Merchant Readiness pivots, aligning edit-time triage with the scoped setup and form workspaces
- `Completed foundation`: business communication details plus scoped email/channel audit workspaces now preserve `businessId` when handing operators to Support Queue or Merchant Readiness, and Support Queue row-level attention/failed-email actions now carry the affected business into Merchant Readiness instead of reopening the aggregate readiness board
- `Security hardening`: source-contract tests now pin those scoped communication-audit and support-row handoffs, including `asp-route-businessId` coverage for row-level Support Queue and Merchant Readiness pivots
- `Completed foundation`: Mobile Operations now preserves its current `businessId` workspace scope when opening Support Queue from the header, go-live/onboarding rails, onboarding dependency card, and business-member device rows, keeping mobile triage aligned with the selected tenant instead of bouncing to the aggregate support board
- `Completed foundation`: Mobile Operations playbooks are now built with the current `businessId`, so missing-push, business-member-device, and member-lifecycle queue actions keep tenant scope in both table links and explicit playbook buttons
- `Completed foundation`: business member, invitation, owner-override, and subscription playbook follow-up URLs now carry `businessId` into Mobile Operations, Support Queue, and Merchant Readiness, so business-scoped playbook tables no longer reopen global remediation boards for tenant-specific work
- `Completed foundation`: Merchant Readiness playbooks now accept an optional `businessId`, so scoped Support Queue and Merchant Readiness workspaces keep tenant context in approval/setup follow-up buttons while aggregate business lists continue to render global playbook handoffs
- `Completed foundation`: the refreshable Support Queue summary partial now receives the full queue workspace VM and preserves `businessId` through refresh, Merchant Readiness, EmailAudits, Payments, and Mobile Operations handoffs, so scoped support workspaces no longer lose tenant context inside the summary cards
- `Completed foundation`: business list row-level attention badges now open the affected business member, location, edit, or invitation remediation workspace directly instead of bouncing operators back to aggregate readiness filters
- `Completed foundation`: scoped Support Queue, Merchant Readiness, and Mobile Operations workspaces now preserve `businessId` when handing operators into Mobile Operations or refreshing the device filter form, closing another tenant-context loss path in mobile support triage
- `Security hardening`: global Support Queue and Mobile Operations handoffs from permission, role, site-settings, and user fleet-level workspaces now route through explicitly named global URL helpers, so intentional aggregate admin pivots no longer look like missed tenant-scope regressions in source scans
- `Security hardening`: Business Communications and Businesses aggregate dashboards now also use explicit global Support Queue, Merchant Readiness, and Mobile Operations URL helpers, leaving the source scan free of raw aggregate handoffs and making future tenant-scope regressions easier to spot
- `Security hardening`: BusinessCommunications, Businesses, SupportQueue, and MerchantReadiness aggregate Users, EmailAudits, and Payments handoffs now route through explicit global URL helpers, separating intentional fleet-wide pivots from scoped tenant handoffs
- `Security hardening`: Billing, CRM invoice, and order financial workspaces now route intentional aggregate Payments handoffs through explicit global URL helpers, so finance/order payment pivots are distinguishable from business-scoped payment triage
- `Security hardening`: SiteSettings, Users, and BusinessForm global Users/Payments handoffs now route through explicit global URL helpers, leaving filtered user queues and tenant-scoped business remediation links separate from aggregate admin pivots
- `Security hardening`: the EmailAudits workspace now routes its aggregate filter/reset self-navigation through an explicit global EmailAudits URL helper, completing the raw aggregate Users/EmailAudits/Payments HTMX cleanup scan
- `Security hardening`: Billing, Businesses support/readiness, CRM, Orders, and SiteSettings aggregate Refunds, TaxCompliance, Invoices, ShipmentsQueue, and ReturnsQueue handoffs now route through explicit global URL helpers, leaving filtered/scoped operational queues distinguishable from fleet-wide pivots
- `Security hardening`: Billing Webhooks, CRM Customers/Overview, and Orders Index aggregate self-navigation now also use explicit global URL helpers, keeping no-arg Webhooks, Customers, Crm Index, and Orders Index pivots separate from filtered queue links
- `Security hardening`: Business Communications Index/ChannelAudits and Billing finance self-navigation now use explicit global URL helpers for aggregate Index, ChannelAudits, FinancialAccounts, Expenses, JournalEntries, and Plans pivots while business-scoped and queue-filtered links remain route-value based
- `Completed foundation`: the lower-traffic finance playbooks in `BillingController` now also render through `SharedResource` keys for financial-account, expense, and journal-entry review lanes, so admin finance workbench localization no longer stops at plans/payments/webhooks while these support queues still keep hard-coded English guidance
- `Completed foundation`: the Quill-based CMS page editor now also localizes its placeholder text and image-upload failure alert instead of keeping raw English copy in the shared page-editor script, so the lower-traffic content-authoring chrome stays on the same admin resource path.

### Primary focus

- `Completed foundation`: complete `Darwin.WebAdmin` as the first operational control center
- `Completed foundation`: support real onboarding and day-one operations for small and medium businesses
- `Completed foundation`: make backend + admin workflows sufficient for `Darwin.Mobile.Business` early operational usage

### Phase-1 provider decisions

- `Completed foundation`: payment implementation is now `Stripe-first` through Stripe-only storefront/member payment-intent normalization, Stripe-specific checkout handoff configuration, explicit Stripe payment-intent/session correlation, webhook verification and lifecycle processing, and Stripe-oriented admin reconciliation/support rails
- `Completed foundation`: shipping implementation is now `DHL-first` on the live storefront quote/checkout path, with DHL-only rating/filtering in the shared shipment-rate handler, DHL-driven selection in checkout intent/order placement, and source-guarded shipping contracts so storefront shipping no longer depends on generic multi-carrier assumptions during the current phase
- `Future / Later phase`: additional payment providers and market-specific payment methods
- `Future / Later phase`: additional shipping/logistics providers

## 2. Go-Live Critical

### Authentication and account lifecycle

- `Completed foundation`: signup, invitation, activation, forgot-password, and reset-password operational flows now have a real cross-surface foundation across WebAdmin, Darwin.Web, Darwin.Mobile.Consumer, and Darwin.Mobile.Business instead of stopping at isolated support actions or resend-only affordances
- `Completed`: WebAdmin now supports lock/unlock, admin email confirmation override, and password-reset initiation support for operator troubleshooting
- `Completed`: platform now has a real confirm-email token flow plus resend-activation email issuance via public auth endpoints and WebAdmin support actions
- `Completed`: password sign-in now enforces account lockout and email-confirmation state for phase-1 activation policy
- `Completed`: consumer registration no longer auto-signs-in when confirmation is pending; it now waits for email confirmation explicitly
- `Completed`: consumer and business mobile login screens now provide self-service activation email requests against the canonical member-auth route
- `Completed`: business-app token refresh now preserves preferred business context during onboarding-safe refresh cycles
- `Completed`: business-facing WebApi access-state enforcement now includes active membership plus user active/email-confirmed/lockout state, so billing/account/loyalty mobile and admin-backed support workflows no longer rely on business status alone
- `Completed foundation`: `Darwin.Mobile.Business` now consumes the richer access-state snapshot with blocker-specific operator guidance for membership, account activation, lockout, and setup debt, so onboarding-safe access no longer collapses into one generic blocked-operations warning
- `Completed foundation`: the `WebAdmin` account-auth surface now hardens login, 2FA, passkey, and registration failure feedback behind localized fallback rails instead of reflecting raw handler error payloads into the admin sign-in UI
- `Completed foundation`: the same `WebAdmin` 2FA sign-in path now also preserves posted challenge state on validation or stamp failures, so retrying a code inside the admin login flow no longer drops `userId`, `rememberMe`, or `returnUrl` context
- `Completed foundation`: `Darwin.Mobile.Consumer` now carries the entered email from forgot-password into the reset-password completion screen, removing a repeated-input detour in the self-service recovery flow
- `Completed foundation`: `Darwin.Mobile.Consumer` reset-password completion now also accepts prefilling email and token from query-style recovery handoff parameters (`email`, `token`, `resetToken`, `code`), so future app-link or routed recovery entry does not depend only on manual copy/paste into the form
- `Completed foundation`: `Darwin.Mobile.Consumer` registration now hands the entered email and pending-activation context back into the login screen, so signup-confirmation follow-up can continue with a prefilled sign-in identity and immediate activation-email resend affordance instead of dropping users back into a blank login form
- `Completed foundation`: `Darwin.Mobile.Consumer` now also has a dedicated activation surface with query-prefilled email/token support plus request-confirmation and confirm-email actions, so the activation lifecycle no longer stops at resend-only affordances on login/register and can accept app-link style token handoff directly
- `Completed foundation`: `Darwin.Mobile.Business` invitation acceptance now also accepts query-prefilled token aliases (`token`, `invitationToken`, `invitation`, `code`) with trim/decode normalization instead of depending on one exact Shell query name, so routed or app-link onboarding handoff is less brittle
- `Completed foundation`: the lower-traffic WebAdmin media-library queue now also resolves filter labels, ops playbooks, and upload validation/editor fallback errors through shared admin resources instead of hard-coded English controller literals, so that operator-side media hygiene no longer falls outside the active bilingual baseline
- `Completed foundation`: the lower-traffic WebAdmin warehouse and supplier queues now also resolve queue filters and ops playbooks through shared admin resources instead of hard-coded controller copy, so inventory setup and procurement-support triage stay inside the same bilingual operator baseline
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web now surfaces equivalent self-service resend-activation UX inline on account hub, sign-in, register, and password-recovery routes, all reusing the canonical activation-request endpoint instead of hiding recovery behind the dedicated activation page
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web now treats the seeded CMS `Footer` menu as the authoritative runtime footer when available, keeps only storefront/legal links in fallback footer mode, resolves Home spotlight degraded messages before rendering them, and seeds fuller bilingual Germany-oriented starter content for `impressum`, `datenschutz`, `agb`, and `widerruf`
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web now uses shopper-friendly shared fallback copy for degraded public API states instead of raw infrastructure wording, and the seeded authoritative footer navigation also includes `Kontakt/Contact` alongside the main legal pages
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public CMS and catalog set loaders now normalize and cache full-set expansion per canonical query tuple, so shared browse/detail/inventory routes no longer widen the same matching public set multiple times during one request tree
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public API cache policy now also exposes one canonical cache-identity helper for normalized path, revalidate window, and key/path tags, so public fetch wiring no longer has to rebuild those cache-identity pieces in parallel
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public API fetch wiring now also reuses one canonical helper for GET cache options versus mutation no-store behavior, so cache policy and fetch-mode decisions no longer drift apart inside public JSON fetch paths
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public API fetch wiring now also reuses one canonical request-plan helper for normalized path, request URL, and fetch cache mode, so path/url/cache assembly no longer has to be rebuilt inline inside the public JSON fetch path
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also uses canonical helpers for request headers and cached GET keys, with direct unit coverage, so request-shape and cache-key behavior are less likely to drift behind inline fetch code
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also uses canonical helpers for failure message-key mapping and degraded result shaping, so shopper-facing fallback copy is less likely to drift behind inline status branches
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also uses canonical helpers for HTTP-status classification and success-result shaping, so response branches are less likely to drift behind inline fetch handling
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also uses a canonical failure-logging policy helper, so degraded public fetches keep one shared rule for which failure kinds stay quiet and which ones emit operational diagnostics
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also uses canonical helpers for response and network diagnostics, so public fetch observability is less likely to drift behind inline response/error branches
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also uses canonical outcome helpers for success, response-failure, invalid-payload, and network-failure branches, with direct unit coverage, so public fetch orchestration is less likely to drift behind inline result-shaping paths
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also uses one canonical failure-logging helper around those shared outcomes, with direct unit coverage, so public fetch observability is less likely to drift behind inline log/no-log branches
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also uses canonical helpers for request-init assembly and POST body shaping, with direct unit coverage, so public request execution is less likely to drift behind inline GET/POST wiring
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also uses canonical helpers for execution context and cached GET args, with direct unit coverage, so request URL, normalized path, and cache-wrapper identity are less likely to drift behind inline fetch orchestration
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also uses one canonical response-parser helper for success and invalid-payload branches, with direct unit coverage, so public response handling is less likely to drift behind inline JSON parsing paths
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also routes fetch-success completion through one canonical execution-success helper, with direct unit coverage, so executor branches are less likely to drift behind inline success-finalization logic
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also routes response-context dispatch through one canonical parser helper, with direct unit coverage, so response-failure and payload-parse branches are less likely to drift behind inline parse orchestration
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also routes parsed-failure completion through one canonical failure-result helper, with direct unit coverage, so finalize branches are less likely to drift behind inline failure dispatch
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also routes response-context parse-plus-finalize through one canonical result helper, with direct unit coverage, so execution success branches are less likely to drift behind inline response-result orchestration
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also derives request-context, URL, and init through one canonical execution-plan helper, with direct unit coverage, so executor branches are less likely to drift behind inline execution planning
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also routes fetch dispatch through one canonical execution-plan executor, with direct unit coverage, so request execution is less likely to drift behind inline try/catch orchestration
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also routes WebApi fetch-wrapper shaping through one canonical fetcher helper, with direct unit coverage, so request-init wrapping is less likely to drift behind inline lambda dispatch
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also routes status-based response degradation through one canonical response-status failure helper, with direct unit coverage, so response-failure shaping is less likely to drift behind inline status branches
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public JSON fetch wiring now also routes degraded outcome shaping through one canonical failure-outcome helper, with direct unit coverage, so response/network failure branches are less likely to drift behind duplicate result assembly
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared public-discovery, member-protected, and commerce page-loader cores now accept canonical argument normalization directly, and that normalization path now has direct unit coverage, so cache-key cleanup stays on the reusable family-loader abstraction instead of drifting route family by route family
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared public-discovery, member-protected, and commerce page-loader cores now also emit standardized family diagnostics such as normalization mode plus continuation/auth fallback footprints, and the helper layer behind that telemetry has direct unit coverage
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared member-summary, storefront-continuation, public-storefront, and member-entry loaders now also emit standardized shared-context diagnostics such as normalization mode plus compact dependency footprints, and the helper layer behind that telemetry has direct unit coverage
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared member-summary, storefront-continuation, public-storefront, and member-entry loaders now also reuse one shared-context loader abstraction, so caching plus baseline diagnostic wiring no longer has to drift loader by loader
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO metadata loaders now also accept canonical argument normalization directly, and Home/public-auth/member-route/commerce/CMS/catalog SEO paths now normalize equivalent args before cache-keying so metadata assembly no longer splits on whitespace or non-canonical browse inputs
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO metadata loaders now also emit explicit normalization mode plus alternate-footprint diagnostics, so production tracing can tell whether metadata assembly was canonicalized and whether language alternates were present without reopening route-local SEO wiring
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized public discovery inventory and public sitemap now also reuse one shared localized-discovery loader abstraction, so caching plus baseline diagnostics for multilingual inventory/sitemap paths no longer drift loader by loader
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized discovery and sitemap observation contexts now also canonicalize multilingual culture lists before diagnostics are emitted, so culture-order drift no longer splits the same inventory/sitemap footprint into different telemetry shapes
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web SEO metadata and localized sitemap/detail alternate maps now also canonicalize language-alternate ordering, so equivalent multilingual alternates no longer drift by input order across `hreflang` and sitemap assembly
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO diagnostics now also carry a culture-stable alternate footprint instead of only a raw alternate count, so production tracing can see exactly which multilingual alternates were present on a metadata path
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO diagnostic helpers now also have direct unit coverage for normalization mode, indexability, and alternate-footprint reporting, so metadata telemetry is less likely to drift silently during loader refactors
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared localized sitemap projection now also canonicalizes alternate ordering before emitting sitemap languages, so `hreflang`-style alternates stay aligned between metadata assembly and sitemap output
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized discovery inventory/sitemap loaders now also use standardized base/success diagnostics with direct unit coverage, so this multilingual branch no longer trails the shared SEO/page-loader abstractions in telemetry quality
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized inventory and sitemap health summaries now also emit compact operational footprints, so production tracing can see empty-culture and sitemap-composition state without reopening raw count fields
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public sitemap static-entry assembly now also canonicalizes supported-culture input before emitting localized index routes, so duplicate or reordered culture lists no longer drift the sitemap shape
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized public discovery projection now also has direct unit coverage for skipping invalid items while keeping alternate/sitemap output canonical, so multilingual inventory refactors are less likely to break detail alternates silently
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized inventory health summaries now also emit a compact inventory footprint with direct unit coverage, so multilingual inventory diagnostics can show culture/item/empty-state shape without reopening raw counts
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized inventory and alternates-map health summaries now also emit standardized summary footprints, so route-health can scan these multilingual baselines through one stable operational field per summary
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized discovery inventory and sitemap health summaries now also emit compact summary footprints, so route-health can expose multilingual coverage and sitemap composition in one operational field instead of several separate counters
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized discovery loader diagnostics now also prefer those standardized summary footprints directly, so multilingual success logs stay aligned with route-health instead of falling back to older raw footprint fields
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized discovery loader diagnostics now also emit an explicit `present/empty` state for inventory and sitemap success paths, so multilingual logs say whether discovery content actually existed instead of only listing counters and footprints
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized alternates-map health summaries now also emit a compact footprint with direct unit coverage, so multilingual detail-alternate diagnostics can show item/alternate/multi-culture shape without reopening raw counts
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web culture-list-based observation contexts now also emit a compact culture footprint with direct unit coverage, so multilingual inventory/sitemap telemetry can show the canonical culture set without reopening raw arrays
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web SEO metadata health summaries now also emit a compact alternate-culture footprint with direct unit coverage, so multilingual metadata diagnostics can show the canonical alternate set without reopening raw maps
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web SEO metadata health summaries now also emit a compact indexability-plus-alternates summary footprint, so route-health summaries can be scanned by one operational SEO field instead of several separate metadata flags
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web SEO metadata health summaries now also emit a compact target footprint for canonical path plus indexability, so route-health summaries can identify the affected metadata target without reopening route payloads
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized discovery loader diagnostics now also emit a standardized success-summary footprint with direct unit coverage, so multilingual inventory/sitemap/alternate branches share one operational summary field in logs
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO loader diagnostics now also emit a standardized success-summary footprint with direct unit coverage, so metadata success logs can be scanned by one compact operational field instead of several separate flags
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO loader diagnostics now also emit a compact target footprint for canonical path plus indexability, so production logs can identify the affected metadata target without reopening route payloads
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO loader diagnostics now also reuse the standardized route-health SEO summaries directly, so success logs and health summaries stay aligned on one metadata truth instead of parallel formatting paths
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO diagnostics now also keep the `noindex / no-alternates` branch under direct test coverage, so private-route metadata telemetry is less likely to drift silently from the canonical SEO summaries
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized discovery health summaries now also emit one canonical `present / empty` state for inventory, alternates, and sitemap branches, so multilingual loader diagnostics can reuse route-health state instead of re-deriving it from raw counters
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO health summaries now also emit the canonical `languageAlternateState`, so loader diagnostics can reuse route-health alternate presence directly instead of re-deriving it from counts
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO health summaries now also emit the canonical alternate summary footprint, so loader diagnostics can reuse route-health alternate formatting directly instead of rebuilding it locally
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO health summaries now also emit canonical `indexability`, so loader diagnostics can reuse the route-health visibility state directly instead of re-deriving it from `noIndex`
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO alternate helpers now also reuse the canonical metadata summary model, so alternate-footprint formatting no longer lives in a parallel helper path
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized discovery health summaries now also emit a canonical detail footprint for inventory, alternates, and sitemap branches, so multilingual loader diagnostics can reuse one operational detail field instead of branch-specific footprint names
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web direct unit coverage now also exercises private/single-locale SEO summaries and the empty sitemap summary branch, so the canonical shared health model is less likely to drift silently in non-public or empty-state scenarios
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web localized discovery loader diagnostics now also have direct unit coverage for canonical detail-footprint preference and explicit empty-detail fallback, so multilingual telemetry is less likely to drift when branch-local footprint fields are refactored
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO health summaries now also emit a compact visibility footprint, so production diagnostics can scan `indexable/localized`, `indexable/single-locale`, or `noindex/private` state without combining multiple fields by hand
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared SEO success diagnostics now also emit an explicit metadata state such as `private`, `localized`, or `single-locale`, so production logs can classify SEO paths faster than by combining indexability and alternate flags by hand
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web SEO metadata health summaries now also emit that same explicit metadata state, so route-health and diagnostics classify SEO paths through one shared model instead of parallel route-local rules
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared route diagnostics now emit compact degraded-surface footprints for partial-health successes, so production telemetry can point directly at affected storefront surfaces instead of only raw `...Status` keys
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web shared API diagnostics now classify failures by API kind, surface family/area, attention level, and suggested action, so production telemetry can point directly at the affected operational surface instead of only raw transport metadata
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web member portal GET reads now reuse a shared request-tree cache layer, so dashboard/summary/history/detail routes no longer duplicate the same canonical member fetches inside one render tree
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web storefront account/auth/commerce windows now reuse one shared spotlight-selection model for CMS pages, category lanes, and strongest product opportunities, so content-driven follow-up no longer drifts surface by surface
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web storefront account/auth/commerce windows now also reuse shared campaign-card and offer-card projection helpers, so CMS/category/product storytelling no longer rebuilds the same campaign narrative route by route
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web public account hub, protected auth-required gates, and cart/checkout auth handoff now also reuse those shared offer-card projections, so entry and recovery routes no longer drift away from the same campaign and next-buy narrative
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web Home now also reuses shared offer-card and category-spotlight projections for its live offer board and category campaign board, so the storefront entry route no longer keeps a separate route-local storytelling model for those core content-and-commerce web parts
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web product detail now also carries a product-composition window that turns the current route into an explicit browse/review/conversion journey plus route map, so public commerce routes no longer stop at detail panels, related cards, and cross-surface rails alone
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web order confirmation now also carries a confirmation-composition window that turns the after-purchase route into an explicit payment/account/storefront journey plus route map, so confirmation no longer stops at receipt panels, payment summaries, and storefront opportunity rails alone
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web profile, preferences, and addresses now also carry a shared self-service composition window that turns those member routes into an explicit current-task/next-step/storefront journey plus route map, so self-service no longer stops at forms, readiness boxes, and storefront side windows alone
- `Completed`: Darwin.Web security now also joins that shared self-service composition window, so the main authenticated account editor routes can all hand off through explicit current-task/next-step/storefront journeys instead of leaving password work as an isolated branch

### Communication Core (email-first MVP)

- `Completed foundation`: the minimum viable email-first Communication Core is now live through the shared application/infrastructure path, with configured subject/body templates, culture-aware default rendering, subject-prefix and test-inbox policy, and persisted `EmailDispatchAudit` rows for invitation, activation, and password-reset flows
- `Completed foundation`: signup-triggered activation email, explicit account-activation resend, business invitation issue/resend, forgot-password initiation, reset-password support, and the current important account-notification baseline now run through the same email-first communication path instead of fragmenting into per-feature ad hoc sending
- `Completed foundation`: business invitation emails no longer stop at simple one-off SMTP composition; they now use the shared transactional template renderer, site-setting-backed templates, culture-aware fallback defaults, recipient-override notice handling, and flow-tagged delivery auditing
- `Completed foundation`: phase-1 Communication Core admin support now includes template visibility, delivery history context, severity/backlog triage, controlled retry for failed or pending invitation, activation, and password-reset rows, policy-aware retry state (`ready`, `cooldown`, `rate-limited`, blocked reason, recent-chain volume), exact-chain exploration for one recipient/flow/business path, provider-backed SMS/WhatsApp transport test sends with customizable diagnostic templates, canonical SMS/WhatsApp phone-verification flows with persisted preferred-channel/fallback policy plus customizable text templates, and a persisted SMS/WhatsApp audit baseline for live verification and operator-diagnostic sends, so the `WebAdmin` support workbench itself is no longer the missing piece
- `Completed foundation`: Communication Core delivery audits now also persist richer operator-grade metadata across email, SMS, and WhatsApp rows, including template key, correlation key, intended recipient versus effective recipient, and provider message id where the provider returns one, and the `Business Communications` audit workspaces now search, group, exact-chain drill in, and render against that richer metadata instead of relying only on raw recipient and status fields
- `Completed foundation`: admin-side communication test email dispatch now also has a persisted outbox floor through `EmailDispatchOperation`, `Darwin.Worker` processing, and SMTP-backed replay into the existing `EmailDispatchAudit` path, so the safest operator-triggered email lane no longer depends only on direct request-path SMTP delivery while broader Communication Core outbox/provider abstraction is still maturing
- `Completed foundation`: admin-side communication test SMS and WhatsApp dispatch now also run through a persisted `ChannelDispatchOperation` queue plus `Darwin.Worker` background processing, with the existing Twilio/Meta sender rails still writing into `ChannelDispatchAudit`, so operator-triggered channel tests no longer depend on direct request-path provider calls while broader Communication Core abstraction is still maturing
- `Planned / Near-term`: deeper outbox/provider abstraction and richer delivery-log modeling still need to move Communication Core beyond the current phase-1 support/admin surface
- `Completed foundation`: the non-email communication workbench now also exposes live SMS/WhatsApp message-family context both in exact-chain incident mode and in the main workspace/profile views, including effective template text, rendered sample preview, supported tokens, target path, policy note, safe-usage guidance, rollout boundary, direct handoff back into the relevant site-settings fragment, and family-level operator actions for verification-audit drill-in and safe diagnostic test reruns, so operators can understand and act on live verification and diagnostic messaging without reconstructing template context from separate screens or guessing whether a family is safe for broader use
- `Completed foundation`: the non-email audit queue now also exposes `Heavy Chains` triage with per-row chain volume/profile context and a dedicated subset, so recurring SMS/WhatsApp delivery stress is easier to separate from isolated verification or diagnostic incidents

### Payment integration

- `Completed foundation`: storefront and member payment-intent flows are now Stripe-first instead of generic, with Stripe-only provider normalization, Stripe-specific checkout-base configuration, Stripe-oriented handoff URLs carrying checkout-session/payment-intent references, and source-guarded controller/builder contracts so hosted checkout no longer falls back to the old generic `DarwinCheckout` payment path
- `Completed foundation`: payment aggregates, storefront payment-intent flows, member/storefront payment projections, and hosted-checkout URL shaping now carry explicit provider payment-intent and checkout-session references alongside the legacy provider transaction reference, so Stripe-oriented correlation can evolve without overloading one generic field or breaking existing clients
- `Completed foundation`: WebAdmin billing payment queues, refund queues, payment editing, and billing-management query/filter logic now also carry explicit provider payment-intent and checkout-session references alongside the legacy provider transaction reference, and Stripe reconciliation/support triage treats any of those identifiers as valid correlation evidence, so operator support no longer loses newer Stripe identifiers behind one generic admin field
- `Completed foundation`: Stripe webhook handling now has a real inbound verification and lifecycle floor through a public `Darwin.WebApi` callback endpoint, Stripe-signature verification against site settings, idempotent `EventLog` recording, and bounded payment/subscription/invoice lifecycle updates for checkout-session, payment-intent, refund, and subscription invoice events, so Stripe callback processing no longer stops at admin-side observability alone
- `Completed foundation`: WebAdmin now exposes Stripe provider-reference state, payment/event history, reconciliation and dispute follow-up rails, plus webhook exception/dispute audit workspaces, so operator support no longer depends on backend-only payment telemetry

### Shipping integration

- `Completed foundation`: generic storefront shipping assumptions have been replaced by a DHL-specific floor in the shared rating path, so public shipping quotes and checkout-intent selection no longer surface non-DHL carriers as the phase-1 operational baseline
- `Completed foundation`: DHL tracking visibility and delivery lifecycle handling now run through shared shipment projections, computed DHL tracking URLs, last-carrier-event metadata, overdue/return diagnostics, and admin/member shipment surfaces, so delivery follow-up no longer stops at raw tracking numbers or queue-only heuristics
- `Completed foundation`: shipment records now also persist carrier-side shipment reference, optional carrier label URL, and a last-carrier-event key, and the admin shipment create flow plus DHL review queues surface that metadata directly, so carrier-side creation/callback context no longer depends only on free-form tracking numbers or inferred event state
- `Completed foundation`: DHL shipment lifecycle callbacks now also have a real signed inbound floor through a public `Darwin.WebApi` webhook endpoint plus `ApplyShipmentCarrierEventHandler` status application, so carrier events can update shipment tracking, label URL, last-event key, and delivered/returned state without staying trapped in manual admin edits alone
